Not all practitioners will encounter Objects 2-10, but when they do arise, they require **specific understanding** and **skillful handling**.

> "The First Object is like learning to walk. The conditional objects are like learning to run, climb, and dance. Each requires its own skill."

### 2. Subtle Attachments Remain

Even after initial breakthrough, **subtle forms** of attachment persist:
-   Attachment to emptiness
-   Attachment to meditative states
-   Attachment to the method itself
-   Attachment to non-attachment

### 3. Integration Is Required

The Ten Modes must become **spontaneous** rather than deliberate:
-   From technique to nature
-   From effort to effortlessness
-   From practice to realization

---

## The Relationship Between Fascicles 3 and 4

| Aspect | Fascicle 3 | Fascicle 4 |
|---|---|---|
| **Focus** | Foundation | Depth |
| **Objects** | Object 1 (detailed), Objects 2-10 (overview) | Objects 2-10 (detailed) |
| **Modes** | Complete exposition | Advanced applications |
| **Obstacles** | Common difficulties | Complex difficulties |
| **Level** | Beginning to intermediate | Intermediate to advanced |

---

## Key Themes in Fascicle 4

### Theme 1: The Afflictions Object (煩惱境)

**When it arises**: Strong afflictions that cannot be resolved through aggregate contemplation alone.

**What Fascicle 4 adds**:
-   Detailed classification of afflictions (根本煩惱 vs. 隨煩惱)
-   Specific methods for each type
-   The relationship between afflictions and Buddha-nature
-   Advanced insight: afflictions as the path

> "In the Perfect Teaching, afflictions are not obstacles to be removed but Buddha-nature to be recognized."

### Theme 2: The Illness Object (病患境)

**When it arises**: Physical sickness interfering with practice.

**What Fascicle 4 adds**:
-   Four types of illness (element imbalance, karmic, demonic, practice-induced)
-   Detailed remedies for each type
-   Using illness as a teacher
-   The non-duality of health and sickness

> "Illness reveals attachment to the body. When seen clearly, illness becomes medicine."

### Theme 3: Karmic Impressions and Demonic Interference (業相境・魔事境)

**When they arise**: Past karma or Māra manifesting during practice.

**What Fascicle 4 adds**:
-   Distinguishing karmic visions from genuine insight
-   The four types of Māra in detail
-   Protective practices
-   The ultimate remedy: seeing all as empty

> "Karma and Māra have no power over one who sees emptiness. They are like shadows—substantial in appearance, empty in nature."

### Theme 4: Meditative States (禪定境)

**When it arises**: Attainment of dhyāna or other absorptions.

**What Fascicle 4 adds**:
-   The four dhyānas and four formless absorptions in detail
-   The danger of attachment to blissful states
-   Distinguishing dhyāna from prajñā
-   Using meditative states as objects of contemplation

> "Dhyāna is concentration. Prajñā is wisdom. Concentration without wisdom is blindness. Wisdom without concentration is instability. The Perfect Teaching unites both."

---

## The Advanced Application of the Ten Modes

In Fascicle 3, the Ten Modes were presented **systematically**. In Fascicle 4, they are applied **flexibly**:

### Systematic vs. Flexible Application

| Approach | When Used | Characteristic |
|---|---|---|
| **Systematic** | Beginning practice | Apply all ten modes in order |
| **Flexible** | Advanced practice | Apply only the modes needed |

**Miao-lo's guidance**:
> "Sharp practitioners may only need Mode 1 (Inconceivable Object). Average practitioners will need Modes 1-5. Those encountering obstacles will need Modes 6-7. All must understand Modes 8-10."

### The Integration of Modes

At advanced levels, the Ten Modes are no longer **ten separate practices** but **one integrated awareness**:

-   **Mode 1** (Inconceivable) becomes the constant background
-   **Mode 2** (Bodhi-Mind) becomes the constant motivation
-   **Mode 3** (Stabilize) becomes effortless
-   **Modes 4-10** arise spontaneously as needed

---

## Miao-lo's Key Insights for Fascicle 4

### On Conditional Objects
> "Do not seek the conditional objects. Do not avoid them. When they arise, recognize them. When they are absent, do not miss them."

### On Advanced Practice
> "The difference between beginning and advanced practice is not in the method but in the depth. The beginner applies the modes deliberately. The advanced practitioner embodies them naturally."

### On Integration
> "When Zhi and Guan are fully integrated, there is no longer 'practice' and 'non-practice.' Every moment is contemplation. Every action is the path."

---

## What to Expect in Fascicle 4

The remainder of this fascicle will provide:

1.  **Detailed treatment of Objects 2-6** (Afflictions, Illness, Karma, Māra, Dhyāna)
2.  **Advanced applications of the Ten Modes** to these objects
3.  **Resolution of complex obstacles** that arise at intermediate and advanced levels
4.  **Integration practices** for making the method spontaneous

---

## Summary

Fascicle 4 is the bridge between **foundational practice** (Fascicle 3) and **complete mastery** (Fascicles 5-10).

| Fascicle | Stage | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| 3 | Foundation | Learning the method |
| 4 | Development | Deepening the method |
| 5-10 | Mastery | Embodying the method |

**The practitioner's journey**:
1.  **Fascicle 3**: Learn to walk (basic contemplation)
2.  **Fascicle 4**: Learn to run (advanced contemplation)
3.  **Fascicles 5-10**: Learn to fly (spontaneous realization)

---

*End of Fascicle 4 Introduction*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 04 SECTION 01 -->

# Fascicle 4, Section 1: The Afflictions Object in Detail
## Working with Strong Emotions (煩惱境詳解)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: When Afflictions Become the Object

The **Afflictions Object** (煩惱境 *Fan Nao Jing*) arises when strong afflictions—greed, anger, delusion—cannot be resolved through aggregate contemplation alone. This is the second of the Ten Objects and the first of the conditional objects.

Miao-lo emphasizes:
> "The Afflictions Object is not a failure of practice. It is a natural development for practitioners with deep karmic roots in affliction. When it arises, it becomes the primary object of contemplation."

---

## Classification of Afflictions

### The Two Main Categories

| Category | Chinese | Number | Nature |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Root Afflictions** | 根本煩惱 (*Gen Ben Fan Nao*) | 6 | Primary defilements |
| **Secondary Afflictions** | 隨煩惱 (*Sui Fan Nao*) | 20 | Derivative defilements |

---

## The Six Root Afflictions (根本煩惱)

### 1. Greed (貪 *Tan*)

**Definition**: Craving, desire, attachment to pleasant objects

**Manifestations**:
-   Sensual desire (欲貪)
-   Material greed (財貪)
-   Attachment to views (見貪)
-   Attachment to existence (有貪)

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Desire for pleasant meditative states
-   Attachment to spiritual experiences
-   Craving for attainment

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Observe** the arising of greed
2.  **Recognize** it as empty of inherent existence
3.  **See** that the object of greed is also empty
4.  **Realize** that greed itself is Buddha-nature

> "Greed is not other than emptiness. When you see greed clearly, you see the Dharma-realm."

---

### 2. Anger (瞋 *Chen*)

**Definition**: Aversion, hostility, rejection of unpleasant objects

**Manifestations**:
-   Anger toward people
-   Anger toward circumstances
-   Anger toward oneself
-   Anger toward the teaching

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Frustration with lack of progress
-   Aversion to obstacles
-   Anger at distractions
-   Hostility toward difficult teachings

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Observe** the arising of anger
2.  **Recognize** it has no fixed essence
3.  **See** that the object of anger is empty
4.  **Realize** that anger is the energy of wisdom distorted

> "Anger is like fire. It can burn or illuminate. When seen as empty, anger becomes the fire of wisdom."

---

### 3. Delusion (癡 *Chi*)

**Definition**: Ignorance, confusion, not seeing things as they are

**Manifestations**:
-   Fundamental ignorance (無明)
-   Confusion about cause and effect
-   Misunderstanding the teaching
-   Not recognizing Buddha-nature

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Confusion about the method
-   Inability to distinguish truth from delusion
-   Misinterpreting experiences
-   Clinging to wrong views

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Recognize** the presence of delusion
2.  **Study** the teachings to clarify understanding
3.  **Contemplate** dependent origination
4.  **Realize** that even delusion is empty

> "Delusion is like darkness. It has no substance. When the light of wisdom shines, darkness disappears."

---

### 4. Pride (慢 *Man*)

**Definition**: Arrogance, sense of superiority

**Seven Types**:
| Type | Chinese | Manifestation |
|---|---|---|
| Simple pride | 慢 | "I am better than equals" |
| Greater pride | 過慢 | "I am better than superiors" |
| Pride of pride | 慢過慢 | "I am the absolute best" |
| Self-pride | 我慢 | "I am" (attachment to self) |
| Inferior pride | 卑慢 | "I am only slightly inferior" |
| False pride | 邪慢 | Pride in non-attainments |
| Perverse pride | 增上慢 | Pride in wrong things |

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Pride in spiritual attainments
-   Comparing oneself to others
-   Attachment to one's own understanding
-   Dismissing other teachings

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Study the Six Identities** to understand stages clearly
2.  **Contemplate the elements** (earth, water, fire, wind) to see the body as impersonal
3.  **Serve others** to cultivate humility
4.  **Realize** that pride is empty

> "Pride is the last fetter. Even advanced practitioners must watch for it. The antidote is seeing that all beings are inherently Buddha."

---

### 5. Doubt (疑 *Yi*)

**Definition**: Uncertainty, lack of confidence in the teaching

**Types**:
-   Doubt about the teaching
-   Doubt about the teacher
-   Doubt about one's own capacity
-   Doubt about causality

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Questioning the validity of the method
-   Uncertainty about progress
-   Wavering between different approaches
-   Intellectual over-analysis

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Study the scriptures** to deepen understanding
2.  **Seek guidance** from qualified teachers
3.  **Contemplate dependent origination** to see the logic of causality
4.  **Develop faith** through practice and results

> "Doubt is like standing at a crossroads. Choose a path and walk it with confidence. Standing still gets you nowhere."

---

### 6. Wrong Views (惡見 *E Jian*)

**Definition**: Mistaken intellectual understandings

**Five Types**:
| Type | Chinese | Error |
|---|---|---|
| View of self | 身見 | Believing in permanent self |
| Extreme views | 邊見 | Eternalism or nihilism |
| Wrong views | 邪見 | Denying causality |
| View-attachment | 見取見 | Clinging to inferior views as supreme |
| Precept-attachment | 戒禁取見 | Clinging to wrong practices |

**How it arises in practice**:
-   Misunderstanding emptiness as nihilism
-   Clinging to one-sided views
-   Attachment to conceptual understanding
-   Mistaking technique for realization

**Contemplation method**:
1.  **Study the Middle Way** to avoid extremes
2.  **Deconstruct all views** systematically (Mode 4)
3.  **Contemplate the Three Truths** to see the complete picture
4.  **Realize** that even views are empty

> "Views are like chains. Even golden chains bind. The Middle Way is freedom from all views."

---

## The Twenty Secondary Afflictions (隨煩惱)

These arise from the six root afflictions and include:

### Small Secondary Afflictions (10)
Anger, resentment, concealment, spite, jealousy, stinginess, deceit, fraud, arrogance, harmfulness

### Medium Secondary Afflictions (2)
Shamelessness, lack of conscience

### Great Secondary Afflictions (8)
Restlessness, torpor, disbelief, laziness, carelessness, forgetfulness, distraction, non-discernment

---

## Applying the Ten Modes to Afflictions

### Mode 1: Contemplate the Inconceivable

**See the affliction as the Three Truths**:
-   **Empty**: The affliction has no inherent existence
-   **Conventional**: The affliction provisionally appears
-   **Middle**: The affliction is neither empty nor existent

> "When you see anger as the Three Truths, anger becomes the Dharma-realm."

### Mode 2: Generate Bodhi-Mind

**Vow**: "I vow to help all beings who suffer from this affliction."

This transforms the affliction from a personal problem into a universal concern.

### Mode 3: Stabilize the Mind

**Use the affliction as the object**:
-   **Zhi**: Calm the mind while the affliction is present
-   **Guan**: Observe the nature of the affliction

### Mode 4: Break Through

**Deconstruct views about the affliction**:
-   "This affliction is mine" → empty
-   "This affliction is real" → empty
-   "I must eliminate this affliction" → empty
-   "Afflictions are obstacles" → empty

### Mode 5: Discern Openness and Obstruction

**What opens the way**:
-   Seeing afflictions as empty
-   Recognizing afflictions as Buddha-nature
-   Using afflictions as the path

**What obstructs**:
-   Suppressing afflictions
-   Indulging afflictions
-   Identifying with afflictions

---

## The Perfect Teaching's View of Afflictions

In the Perfect Teaching, afflictions are not obstacles to be removed but **Buddha-nature to be recognized**.

### The Three Levels of Understanding

| Level | View | Practice |
|---|---|---|
| **Tripiṭaka** | Afflictions are enemies | Eliminate them |
| **Shared/Distinct** | Afflictions are empty | See through them |
| **Perfect** | Afflictions are Buddha-nature | Recognize them |

### The Key Insight

> "Afflictions and Bodhi are not two. When you see afflictions clearly, you see Buddha-nature. This is not suppression. This is not transformation. This is recognition."

---

## Summary

The Afflictions Object requires:
1.  **Recognition** of which affliction has arisen
2.  **Classification** (root or secondary)
3.  **Application** of the Ten Modes
4.  **Realization** that afflictions are Buddha-nature

**Miao-lo's final point**:
> "The practitioner who works with the Afflictions Object deeply will realize that afflictions are the swiftest path to enlightenment. Why? Because they reveal attachment most clearly. When attachment is seen, it dissolves."

---

*End of Fascicle 4, Section 1*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 04 SECTION 02 -->

# Fascicle 4, Section 2: Illness, Karma, and Māra Objects
## Working with Physical and External Obstacles (病患・業相・魔事境)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: Three Related Objects

This section covers three conditional objects that often arise together:
-   **Illness Object** (病患境) — Physical sickness
-   **Karmic Impressions Object** (業相境) — Past karma manifesting
-   **Demonic Interference Object** (魔事境) — Māra's obstacles

These are grouped because they share common characteristics: they arise from **external or karmic causes** rather than from present mental states.

---

## Part 1: The Illness Object (病患境)

### When It Arises

Physical sickness that **interferes with practice** and cannot be resolved through simple rest or medical treatment alone.

Miao-lo distinguishes this from ordinary illness:
> "Ordinary illness is treated with medicine. The Illness Object arises when sickness becomes a teacher, revealing deep attachment to the body."

### The Four Types of Illness

| Type | Chinese | Cause | Treatment |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Element Imbalance** | 四大不調 | Earth, water, fire, wind out of balance | Medical + contemplation |
| **Karmic Illness** | 業病 | Past karma ripening | Contemplation + repentance |
| **Demonic Illness** | 魔病 | Māra's interference | Protection + contemplation |
| **Practice-Induced** | 禪病 | Improper method | Correct the method |

---

### Type 1: Element Imbalance (四大不調)

**The Four Elements**:
-   **Earth** (地): Solidity, structure
-   **Water** (水): Fluidity, cohesion
-   **Fire** (火): Heat, metabolism
-   **Wind** (風): Motion, breath

**Imbalance manifestations**:
| Element | Excess | Deficiency |
|---|---|---|
| Earth | Heaviness, stiffness | Weakness, instability |
| Water | Swelling, dampness | Dryness, dehydration |
| Fire | Fever, inflammation | Coldness, poor circulation |
| Wind | Restlessness, pain | Lethargy, poor breathing |

**Treatment**:
1.  **Medical**: Adjust diet, environment, activity
2.  **Contemplation**: See the elements as empty and impermanent
3.  **Balance**: Regulate the five matters (food, sleep, body, breath, mind)

---

### Type 2: Karmic Illness (業病)

**Definition**: Illness arising from **past negative karma** ripening in the present.

**Signs**:
-   Sudden onset without clear physical cause
-   Resistant to medical treatment
-   Accompanied by karmic visions or memories
-   Intensifies during practice

**Treatment**:
1.  **Repentance** (懺悔): Acknowledge past actions
2.  **Contemplation**: See karma as empty
3.  **Merit dedication**: Transfer merit to those harmed
4.  **Patience**: Endure with understanding

**The contemplation**:
> "Past karma is like a seed. It has no power until conditions ripen it. When you see karma as empty, the seed loses its power to sprout."

---

### Type 3: Demonic Illness (魔病)

**Definition**: Illness caused by **Māra's interference** to obstruct practice.

**Signs**:
-   Sudden, severe onset during intensive practice
-   Accompanied by disturbing visions or thoughts
-   Disappears when practice stops
-   Returns when practice resumes

**Treatment**:
1.  **Protective practices**: Mantras, precepts, refuge
2.  **Contemplate emptiness**: See all phenomena as empty
3.  **Do not engage**: Ignore visions and disturbances
4.  **Seek guidance**: Consult experienced teachers

---

### Type 4: Practice-Induced Illness (禪病)

**Definition**: Illness arising from **improper meditation technique**.

**Common causes**:
-   Forcing concentration
-   Improper breathing
-   Wrong posture
-   Excessive effort
-   Imbalanced Zhi and Guan

**Treatment**:
1.  **Correct the method**: Adjust technique
2.  **Rest**: Temporarily reduce practice intensity
3.  **Regulate**: Balance the five matters
4.  **Seek guidance**: Learn proper technique

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Illness

**Mode 1 (Inconceivable)**: See illness as the Three Truths
-   Empty: No inherent existence
-   Conventional: Appears with causes and conditions
-   Middle: Neither existent nor non-existent

**Mode 2 (Bodhi-Mind)**: "I vow to help all beings who suffer from illness"

**Mode 3 (Stabilize)**: Use pain as the object of contemplation

**Key insight**:
> "Illness is not other than Buddha-nature. When you see pain clearly, you see the Dharma-realm. This is not suppressing pain. This is recognizing its true nature."

---

## Part 2: The Karmic Impressions Object (業相境)

### When It Arises

Past karma manifesting as **visions, memories, or experiences** during meditation.

### Types of Karmic Manifestations

| Type | Manifestation | Response |
|---|---|---|
| **Past Life Visions** | Seeing previous existences | Do not engage |
| **Karmic Memories** | Remembering past actions | Observe without attachment |
| **Karmic Debts** | Sensing obligations | Contemplate emptiness |
| **Future Visions** | Seeing potential futures | Recognize as conditional |

---

### The Danger of Engagement

**Do not**:
-   Become fascinated with visions
-   Identify with past lives
-   Become disturbed by karmic memories
-   Cling to pleasant visions
-   Fear unpleasant visions

**Do**:
-   Recognize as karmic manifestation
-   Contemplate as empty
-   Continue with practice
-   Maintain equanimity

> "Karmic visions are like dreams. They have no substance. Do not chase them. Do not flee from them. Simply recognize them as empty."

---

### Distinguishing Karmic Visions from Genuine Insight

| Characteristic | Karmic Vision | Genuine Insight |
|---|---|---|
| **Nature** | Personal, narrative | Universal, direct |
| **Effect** | Fascination or disturbance | Clarity and peace |
| **Content** | Specific events, people | Dharma-nature, emptiness |
| **Result** | Attachment or aversion | Liberation |

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Karmic Impressions

**The key**: **Non-engagement**

1.  **Recognize** it as karmic manifestation
2.  **Contemplate** it as empty
3.  **Do not** identify with it
4.  **Continue** with the practice

> "When karmic visions arise, treat them like clouds passing through the sky. The sky is not affected by clouds. Your Buddha-nature is not affected by karma."

---

## Part 3: The Demonic Interference Object (魔事境)

### The Four Types of Māra

| Type | Chinese | Manifestation | Response |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Affliction-Māra** | 煩惱魔 | Internal afflictions intensifying | Contemplate as empty |
| **Aggregate-Māra** | 陰魔 | Attachment to body-mind | See aggregates as empty |
| **Death-Māra** | 死魔 | Fear of death or impermanence | Contemplate deathlessness |
| **Heavenly-Māra** | 天魔 | External interference | Protective practices |

---

### Affliction-Māra (煩惱魔)

**Manifestation**: Sudden, intense afflictions arising during practice

**Examples**:
-   Overwhelming desire
-   Uncontrollable anger
-   Deep depression
-   Extreme pride

**Response**:
-   Recognize as Māra's work
-   Contemplate the affliction as empty
-   Do not suppress or indulge
-   Apply Mode 1 (Inconceivable)

---

### Aggregate-Māra (陰魔)

**Manifestation**: Extreme attachment to or fear of the body-mind

**Examples**:
-   Fear of losing the self
-   Clinging to physical existence
-   Attachment to mental states
-   Resistance to emptiness

**Response**:
-   Contemplate the aggregates as empty
-   Study the teaching on non-self
-   Develop faith in Buddha-nature
-   Gradual approach to emptiness

---

### Death-Māra (死魔)

**Manifestation**: Fear of death or impermanence

**Examples**:
-   Anxiety about mortality
-   Clinging to life
-   Fear of annihilation
-   Resistance to change

**Response**:
-   Contemplate the deathless (不生不滅)
-   Understand emptiness does not mean annihilation
-   See death as transformation, not ending
-   Realize Buddha-nature is unborn and undying

---

### Heavenly-Māra (天魔)

**Manifestation**: External interference from Māra or his retinue

**Examples**:
-   Disturbing visions
-   Voices or sounds
-   Physical sensations
-   Environmental disturbances

**Response**:
1.  **Do not fear**: Fear gives Māra power
2.  **Do not engage**: Ignore visions and voices
3.  **Protective practices**: Mantras, precepts, refuge
4.  **Contemplate emptiness**: See all as empty
5.  **Seek guidance**: Consult teachers if needed

---

### The Ultimate Remedy for All Māra

**Contemplate emptiness**:
> "Māra has no power over one who sees emptiness. Like a shadow, Māra appears substantial but is empty in nature. When you shine the light of wisdom, shadows disappear."

**The Perfect Teaching's view**:
> "Māra is not other than Buddha. When you see Māra clearly, you see Buddha-nature. This is why advanced practitioners thank Māra for revealing attachment."

---

## Summary: Working with Physical and External Obstacles

| Object | Primary Approach | Key Insight |
|---|---|---|
| **Illness** | Contemplate pain as Three Truths | Illness reveals attachment to body |
| **Karmic Impressions** | Non-engagement, see as empty | Karma is like dreams—no substance |
| **Demonic Interference** | Contemplate emptiness, protective practices | Māra has no power over emptiness |

**Miao-lo's final point**:
> "These three objects—illness, karma, and Māra—are often feared by practitioners. But in the Perfect Teaching, they are recognized as teachers. They reveal attachment most clearly. When attachment is seen, it dissolves."

---

*End of Fascicle 4, Section 2*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 04 SECTION 03 -->

# Fascicle 4, Section 3: Meditative States and Integration
## The Dhyāna Object and Spontaneous Practice (禪定境與融通)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: The Subtle Danger of Attainment

The **Meditative States Object** (禪定境 *Chan Ding Jing*) arises when the practitioner attains **dhyāna** (禪定) or other meditative absorptions. This is paradoxically both an achievement and a potential obstacle.

Miao-lo warns:
> "Dhyāna is like honey on the razor's edge. Sweet, but dangerous if you linger. The practitioner must recognize dhyāna as a milestone, not the destination."

---

## The Four Dhyānas (四禪)

### First Dhyāna (初禪)

**Characteristics**:
-   Joy and bliss (喜樂) arising from seclusion
-   Thought and examination (尋伺) still present
-   Five factors: Thought, examination, joy, bliss, one-pointedness

**Experience**:
-   Deep peace and happiness
-   Clarity of mind
-   Physical lightness

**Danger**:
-   Attachment to pleasant states
-   Mistaking concentration for wisdom
-   Desire to remain in this state

**Contemplation**:
> "See the first dhyāna as empty, conventional, and middle. It is a conditioned state, not ultimate reality."

---

### Second Dhyāna (二禪)

**Characteristics**:
-   Joy and bliss arising from concentration
-   Thought and examination cease
-   Three factors: Joy, bliss, one-pointedness

**Experience**:
-   Deeper peace than first dhyāna
-   Internal clarity (內淨)
-   Unified mind

**Danger**:
-   Stronger attachment to bliss
-   Pride in attainment
-   Belief that this is liberation

**Contemplation**:
> "The second dhyāna is more subtle than the first, but still conditioned. Do not mistake depth for completeness."

---

### Third Dhyāna (三禪)

**Characteristics**:
-   Equanimity and subtle bliss
-   Joy ceases, only bliss remains
-   Mindfulness and clear comprehension

**Experience**:
-   Profound peace
-   Subtle happiness
-   Refined awareness

**Danger**:
-   Attachment to subtle bliss
-   Belief in having transcended afflictions
-   Stagnation in practice

**Contemplation**:
> "The third dhyāna is the most blissful of all states. This is precisely why it is the most dangerous. Bliss is still a conditioned phenomenon."

---

### Fourth Dhyāna (四禪)

**Characteristics**:
-   Pure equanimity
-   Neither pleasure nor pain
-   Perfect mindfulness and clarity

**Experience**:
-   Complete mental stability
-   Profound equanimity
-   Clear, bright awareness

**Danger**:
-   Attachment to equanimity
-   Mistaking equanimity for wisdom
-   Belief in having attained the goal

**Contemplation**:
> "The fourth dhyāna is the pinnacle of concentration. But concentration is not wisdom. Dhyāna must be united with prajñā."

---

## The Four Formless Absorptions (四無色定)

Beyond the four dhyānas are four formless absorptions:

| Absorption | Chinese | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| **Infinite Space** | 空無邊處 | Boundless space |
| **Infinite Consciousness** | 識無邊處 | Boundless consciousness |
| **Nothingness** | 無所有處 | Nothingness |
| **Neither-Perception-Nor-Non-Perception** | 非想非非想處 | Extremely subtle state |

**The danger**: These are even more subtle than the dhyānas and thus even more seductive. Practitioners can remain in these states for eons without progressing toward liberation.

---

## Distinguishing Dhyāna from Prajñā

| Aspect | Dhyāna (Concentration) | Prajñā (Wisdom) |
|---|---|---|
| **Nature** | Stability, one-pointedness | Insight, understanding |
| **Function** | Calms the mind | Sees the truth |
| **Result** | Peace, bliss | Liberation |
| **Danger** | Attachment to states | Attachment to views |
| **Alone** | Leads to rebirth in form/formless realms | Leads to dry wisdom |
| **Together** | The Perfect Path | — |

**Miao-lo's teaching**:
> "Dhyāna without prajñā is blindness. Prajñā without dhyāna is instability. The Perfect Teaching unites both in every moment."

---

## Applying the Ten Modes to Meditative States

### Mode 1: Contemplate the Inconceivable

**See dhyāna as the Three Truths**:
-   **Empty**: The meditative state has no inherent existence
-   **Conventional**: It arises from causes and conditions
-   **Middle**: It is neither existent nor non-existent

### Mode 2: Generate Bodhi-Mind

**Transform the experience**:
-   "I vow to help all beings attain this peace"
-   "I vow to guide all beings beyond attachment to peace"

### Mode 10: Release Dharma-Attachment

**The critical mode for this object**:
-   Recognize the attainment
-   Appreciate it without clinging
-   Continue toward complete realization
-   Let go of even the letting go

> "When you release attachment to dhyāna, dhyāna becomes a tool rather than a trap."

---

## Integration: Making Practice Spontaneous

The final theme of Fascicle 4 is **integration** (融通 *Rong Tong*)—making the Ten Modes spontaneous rather than deliberate.

### Three Stages of Integration

| Stage | Practice | Characteristic |
|---|---|---|
| **Deliberate** | Consciously applying modes | Effort required |
| **Natural** | Modes arise spontaneously | Effortless |
| **Complete** | No distinction between practice and non-practice | Constant contemplation |

---

### From Technique to Nature

**Deliberate stage** (初學):
-   "I will now apply Mode 1"
-   "I will now generate Bodhi-Mind"
-   Conscious effort

**Natural stage** (純熟):
-   Modes arise without deliberation
-   Like a skilled musician playing naturally
-   Effort becomes effortless

**Complete stage** (究竟):
-   Every moment is contemplation
-   Every action is the path
-   No separation between practice and life

---

### The Integration of Zhi and Guan

**Beginning practice**:
-   Zhi and Guan are practiced separately
-   "Now I calm" / "Now I contemplate"

**Intermediate practice**:
-   Zhi and Guan alternate smoothly
-   Balance is maintained

**Advanced practice**:
-   Zhi and Guan are simultaneous
-   Calming IS contemplating
-   Contemplating IS calming

**Perfect integration**:
> "When Zhi and Guan are fully integrated, there is no longer 'calming' and 'contemplating.' There is only the mind resting in its true nature, which is both still and clear."

---

## Signs of Integration

| Sign | Manifestation |
|---|---|
| **Effortlessness** | Practice feels natural, not forced |
| **Continuity** | Contemplation continues in all activities |
| **Flexibility** | Appropriate response arises spontaneously |
| **Stability** | Mind remains clear in all circumstances |
| **Compassion** | Bodhi-Mind is constant, not cultivated |

---

## The Practitioner's Journey Through Fascicle 4

| Section | Object | Key Learning |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Afflictions | Afflictions are Buddha-nature |
| 2 | Illness/Karma/Māra | External obstacles are teachers |
| 3 | Meditative States | Attainments can be traps |
| 3 | Integration | Make practice spontaneous |

---

## Miao-lo's Final Teaching for Fascicle 4

> "The advanced practitioner does not seek objects. Does not avoid objects. When objects arise, they are recognized and worked with. When objects are absent, there is no sense of loss. This is the meaning of integration."

> "The difference between beginning and advanced practice is not in the method but in the depth. The beginner applies the modes deliberately. The advanced practitioner embodies them naturally. The master has forgotten both practice and non-practice."

---

## Summary

Fascicle 4 completes the treatment of conditional objects and introduces integration:

**Objects covered**:
-   Afflictions (6 root + 20 secondary)
-   Illness (4 types)
-   Karmic Impressions
-   Demonic Interference (4 types of Māra)
-   Meditative States (4 dhyānas + 4 formless absorptions)

**Key insights**:
-   All objects are Buddha-nature
-   Obstacles are teachers
-   Attainments can be traps
-   Practice must become spontaneous

**The path forward**:
-   Fascicles 5-10 will cover the remaining objects (Wrong Views, Pride, Two Vehicles, Bodhisattva) and the ultimate fruit of practice

---

*End of Fascicle 4, Section 3*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 04 CLOSING -->

# Fascicle 4: Closing Summary
## Advanced Applications of Correct Contemplation

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Overview of Fascicle 4

Fascicle 4 bridges the gap between **foundational practice** (Fascicle 3) and **complete mastery** (Fascicles 5-10). It provides detailed treatment of conditional objects and introduces the concept of **integration**—making practice spontaneous.

---

## Summary of Key Sections

### Opening: Introduction to Advanced Practice
-   Transition from foundation to depth
-   Three challenges: conditional objects, subtle attachments, integration
-   **Point**: Advanced practice requires flexibility and spontaneity

### Section 1: Afflictions Object in Detail
-   Six root afflictions (greed, anger, delusion, pride, doubt, wrong views)
-   Twenty secondary afflictions
-   Application of Ten Modes to afflictions
-   **Point**: Afflictions are Buddha-nature to be recognized, not enemies to be destroyed

### Section 2: Illness, Karma, and Māra Objects
-   Four types of illness (element imbalance, karmic, demonic, practice-induced)
-   Karmic impressions and non-engagement
-   Four types of Māra (affliction, aggregate, death, heavenly)
-   **Point**: External obstacles are teachers revealing attachment

### Section 3: Meditative States and Integration
-   Four dhyānas and four formless absorptions
-   Distinguishing dhyāna from prajñā
-   Three stages of integration (deliberate, natural, complete)
-   **Point**: Attainments can be traps; practice must become spontaneous

---

## The Core Teaching of Fascicle 4

**All objects are Buddha-nature**

Whether afflictions, illness, karma, Māra, or meditative states—all phenomena that arise during practice are **manifestations of Buddha-nature**. The practitioner's task is not to eliminate or transcend them but to **recognize their true nature**.

---

## Key Insights

### On Afflictions
> "Afflictions and Bodhi are not two. When you see afflictions clearly, you see Buddha-nature. This is not suppression. This is not transformation. This is recognition."

### On Obstacles
> "Illness, karma, and Māra are often feared by practitioners. But in the Perfect Teaching, they are recognized as teachers. They reveal attachment most clearly. When attachment is seen, it dissolves."

### On Attainments
> "Dhyāna is like honey on the razor's edge. Sweet, but dangerous if you linger. The practitioner must recognize dhyāna as a milestone, not the destination."

### On Integration
> "When Zhi and Guan are fully integrated, there is no longer 'calming' and 'contemplating.' There is only the mind resting in its true nature, which is both still and clear."

---

## The Conditional Objects Covered

| Object | Key Teaching | Treatment |
|---|---|---|
| **Afflictions** | Are Buddha-nature | Detailed (6 root + 20 secondary) |
| **Illness** | Reveals attachment to body | Four types with remedies |
| **Karmic Impressions** | Like dreams, no substance | Non-engagement |
| **Demonic Interference** | No power over emptiness | Four types of Māra |
| **Meditative States** | Can be traps | Four dhyānas + four formless |

**Remaining objects** (to be covered in Fascicles 5-10):
-   Wrong Views (諸見境)
-   Pride (慢境)
-   Two Vehicles (二乘境)
-   Bodhisattva (菩薩境)

---

## The Path of Integration

| Stage | Characteristic | Practice |
|---|---|---|
| **Deliberate** | Conscious application of modes | "I will now apply Mode 1" |
| **Natural** | Spontaneous arising of modes | Modes arise without deliberation |
| **Complete** | No distinction between practice and non-practice | Every moment is contemplation |

---

## Miao-lo's Key Teachings

### On Working with Objects
> "Do not seek the conditional objects. Do not avoid them. When they arise, recognize them. When they are absent, do not miss them."

### On Advanced Practice
> "The difference between beginning and advanced practice is not in the method but in the depth. The beginner applies the modes deliberately. The advanced practitioner embodies them naturally."

### On Mastery
> "The master has forgotten both practice and non-practice. Every moment is contemplation. Every action is the path."

---

## What Comes Next (Fascicles 5-10)

With the major conditional objects covered and integration introduced, the remaining fascicles will:

-   **Fascicles 5-6**: Complete treatment of remaining objects (Wrong Views, Pride, Two Vehicles, Bodhisattva)
-   **Fascicles 7-8**: Fruit and results of practice (果報)
-   **Fascicle 9**: How teaching arises from realization (起教)
-   **Fascicle 10**: Ultimate return to the source (旨歸)

---

## Practical Summary

**For the practitioner at this level**:

1.  **Recognize** which object has arisen
2.  **Apply** the Ten Modes flexibly (not mechanically)
3.  **Work with** the object as Buddha-nature
4.  **Move toward** spontaneous integration
5.  **Release** attachment to all attainments

**The goal**: Not to perfect technique but to **embody the teaching** so completely that technique becomes nature.

---

*End of Fascicle 4 Summary*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 05 OPENING -->

# Fascicle 5: Introduction to Final Objects
## Completing the Ten Objects (十境圓滿)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: The Final Four Objects

Fascicle 5 completes the treatment of the **Ten Objects of Contemplation** by covering the final four conditional objects:

| # | Chinese | English | Nature |
|---|---|---|---|
| 7 | 諸見境 | Wrong Views Object | Intellectual obstacles |
| 8 | 慢境 | Pride Object | Attitudinal obstacles |
| 9 | 二乘境 | Two Vehicles Object | Hīnayāna tendencies |
| 10 | 菩薩境 | Bodhisattva Object | Advanced experiences |

These final objects represent **subtle obstacles** that arise at more advanced stages of practice. Unlike the earlier objects (Afflictions, Illness, Karma, Māra, Dhyāna), which can arise at any level, these four typically manifest when the practitioner has already made significant progress.

---

## Why These Objects Are Last

Miao-lo explains the ordering:
> "The first six objects (Aggregates through Dhyāna) are common obstacles that most practitioners encounter. The final four are subtle obstacles that only advanced practitioners face. They are last not because they are least important, but because they arise last."

### The Progression

| Objects | Stage | Characteristic |
|---|---|---|
| **1-6** | Beginning to Intermediate | Gross obstacles |
| **7-8** | Intermediate to Advanced | Subtle obstacles |
| **9-10** | Advanced | Attainment obstacles |

---

## The Nature of Subtle Obstacles

### Gross vs. Subtle Obstacles

**Gross obstacles** (Objects 1-6):
-   Obvious and recognizable
-   Cause clear disturbance
-   Easier to identify

**Subtle obstacles** (Objects 7-10):
-   Hidden and difficult to recognize
-   May appear as virtues
-   Harder to identify

> "Gross afflictions are like thieves in the open. Subtle obstacles are like thieves in disguise. The latter are more dangerous because they are harder to recognize."

---

## Object 7: Wrong Views (諸見境)

### What It Is

**Wrong Views** arise when the practitioner develops **mistaken intellectual understandings** about the Dharma, often based on partial realization.

### Why It Arises at This Stage

After experiencing emptiness or other insights, the practitioner may:
-   Cling to conceptual understanding
-   Mistake intellectual knowledge for realization
-   Develop one-sided views
-   Become attached to their own interpretation

### The Danger

> "Wrong views at the advanced level are more dangerous than gross afflictions at the beginning level. Why? Because the practitioner believes they have understood, and thus stops progressing."

---

## Object 8: Pride (慢境)

### What It Is

**Pride** arises from **partial attainment**—the practitioner has made genuine progress but mistakes it for complete realization.

### The Seven Types of Pride

| Type | Manifestation at Advanced Level |
|---|---|
| **Simple pride** | "I am more advanced than other practitioners" |
| **Greater pride** | "I am more advanced than my teachers" |
| **Pride of pride** | "I am among the most advanced" |
| **Self-pride** | "I have attained the Dharma" |
| **Inferior pride** | "I am only slightly less advanced than the masters" |
| **False pride** | Pride in non-attainments |
| **Perverse pride** | Pride in wrong attainments |

### Why It's Subtle

At advanced levels, pride often disguises itself as:
-   Confidence in the Dharma
-   Certainty in understanding
-   Authority to teach

> "The most dangerous pride is the pride of having transcended pride."

---

## Object 9: Two Vehicles (二乘境)

### What It Is

The **Two Vehicles Object** arises when the practitioner, despite practicing the Perfect Teaching, develops tendencies toward **Hīnayāna** (śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha paths).

### Manifestations

-   Desire for personal liberation only
-   Weariness with saṃsāra
-   Lack of compassion for beings
-   Satisfaction with partial realization
-   Retreat from bodhisattva vows

### Why It Arises

After experiencing the suffering of saṃsāra deeply and tasting the peace of emptiness, the practitioner may think:
> "Why should I remain in saṃsāra to help others? I could enter nirvāṇa now."

### The Antidote

**Recall the Bodhi-Mind** (Mode 2):
-   Remember the Four Great Vows
-   Cultivate great compassion
-   Study Mahāyāna teachings
-   Engage in bodhisattva practices

---

## Object 10: Bodhisattva (菩薩境)

### What It Is

The **Bodhisattva Object** represents **advanced experiences** on the bodhisattva path—the ten stages (十地), supernatural powers (神通), etc.

### Why It's an "Object"

Even at this advanced level, obstacles can arise:
-   Attachment to bodhisattva attainments
-   Pride in supernatural powers
-   Dharma-attachment to the path itself
-   Subtle clinging to the bodhisattva identity

### The Final Obstacle

> "The bodhisattva who clings to being a bodhisattva has not yet completed the path. Only when even the bodhisattva identity is released does one enter complete Buddhahood."

---

## The Relationship Between the Final Four Objects

These four objects form a **progression of subtle obstacles**:

| Object | Nature | Obstacle |
|---|---|---|
| **Wrong Views** | Intellectual | Clinging to understanding |
| **Pride** | Attitudinal | Clinging to attainment |
| **Two Vehicles** | Motivational | Clinging to personal liberation |
| **Bodhisattva** | Identity | Clinging to the path itself |

---

## Applying the Ten Modes to Subtle Obstacles

### The Challenge

With subtle obstacles, the **first five modes** may not be sufficient. The practitioner must:

1.  **Recognize** the obstacle (often the hardest part)
2.  **Apply Mode 4** (Break Through) to deconstruct subtle views
3.  **Apply Mode 8** (Know the Stages) to avoid pride
4.  **Apply Mode 10** (Release Dharma-Attachment) to let go

### The Key Insight

> "Subtle obstacles are overcome not by adding more practice but by releasing attachment to practice itself. This is why Mode 10 (Release Dharma-Attachment) is critical at this level."

---

## Miao-lo's Teaching on the Final Objects

### On Recognition

> "The hardest part of working with subtle obstacles is recognizing them. Gross afflictions announce themselves. Subtle obstacles disguise themselves as virtues."

### On Humility

> "The practitioner who thinks they have transcended all obstacles is precisely the one who has not. True realization is accompanied by profound humility."

### On Completion

> "When all ten objects have been worked with—when even the bodhisattva path is released—what remains? Not emptiness. Not existence. Not the Middle Way. What remains cannot be spoken."

---

## What to Expect in Fascicle 5

The remainder of this fascicle will provide:

1.  **Detailed treatment** of Wrong Views and Pride (Section 1)
2.  **Detailed treatment** of Two Vehicles and Bodhisattva (Section 2)
3.  **Integration** of all ten objects (Section 3)
4.  **Completion** of the Correct Contemplation chapter

---

## Summary

Fascicle 5 completes the Ten Objects:

**Objects 1-6** (Fascicles 3-4):
-   Aggregates, Afflictions, Illness, Karma, Māra, Dhyāna
-   Gross obstacles for beginning to intermediate practitioners

**Objects 7-10** (Fascicle 5):
-   Wrong Views, Pride, Two Vehicles, Bodhisattva
-   Subtle obstacles for intermediate to advanced practitioners

**The progression**:
-   From gross to subtle
-   From obvious to hidden
-   From easy to recognize to difficult to recognize

**The goal**: Complete liberation through recognizing and releasing all obstacles, even the subtle ones.

---

*End of Fascicle 5 Introduction*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 05 SECTION 01 -->

# Fascicle 5, Section 1: Wrong Views and Pride Objects
## Intellectual and Attitudinal Obstacles (諸見境・慢境)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: Subtle Obstacles of the Mind

This section covers two closely related objects:
- **Wrong Views Object** (諸見境) — Intellectual obstacles
- **Pride Object** (慢境) — Attitudinal obstacles

Both arise from **partial realization** and represent subtle forms of clinging that advanced practitioners must recognize and release.

---

## Part 1: The Wrong Views Object (諸見境)

### When It Arises

The Wrong Views Object arises when the practitioner:
- Has experienced genuine insight
- Develops conceptual understanding based on that insight
- Clings to the conceptual understanding
- Mistakes understanding for complete realization

> "The danger is not in having views, but in clinging to views. Even correct views, when clung to, become obstacles."

---

### The Five Wrong Views (五惡見)

These are the same five views mentioned in Fascicle 4 as part of the sixth root affliction, but here they manifest at a more subtle level.

#### 1. View of Self (身見 *Shen Jian*)

**At the advanced level**:
- Not the gross belief "I am this body"
- But the subtle belief "I am the one who has realized emptiness"
- Clinging to the identity of "realized practitioner"

**Contemplation**:
> "Who is it that has realized? When you search for the realizer, where is it to be found?"

---

#### 2. Extreme Views (邊見 *Bian Jian*)

**Two extremes**:

| Extreme | Manifestation at Advanced Level |
|---|---|
| **Eternalism** | Clinging to Buddha-nature as a permanent entity |
| **Nihilism** | Clinging to emptiness as annihilation |

**The Middle Way**:
- Buddha-nature is neither permanent nor impermanent
- Emptiness is neither existence nor non-existence
- The Middle Way itself must not be clung to

**Contemplation**:
> "The Middle Way is not a third position between two extremes. It is the release of all positions."

---

#### 3. Wrong Views (邪見 *Xie Jian*)

**At the advanced level**:
- Denying the validity of other teachings
- Believing only one's own understanding is correct
- Dismissing practices or methods that don't align with one's experience

**Examples**:
- "Only sudden enlightenment is valid; gradual practice is inferior"
- "Only emptiness is real; conventional truth is delusion"
- "Only the Perfect Teaching is true; other teachings are false"

**Contemplation**:
> "All teachings are skillful means. To cling to one teaching and reject others is to miss the point of all teachings."

---

#### 4. View-Attachment (見取見 *Jian Qu Jian*)

**Definition**: Clinging to inferior views as if they were supreme

**At the advanced level**:
- Clinging to partial realization as complete
- Believing one's current understanding is final
- Attachment to one's own interpretation of the Dharma

**The danger**:
> "The practitioner who believes they have understood everything has understood nothing. True understanding knows its own incompleteness."

---

#### 5. Precept-Attachment (戒禁取見 *Jie Jin Qu Jian*)

**Definition**: Clinging to wrong practices as if they were liberating

**At the advanced level**:
- Rigid adherence to forms without understanding essence
- Believing that technique alone brings liberation
- Attachment to specific methods or practices

**The balance**:
- Precepts and practices are necessary
- But clinging to them is an obstacle
- Use them skillfully, release them when appropriate

---

### Additional Wrong Views at Advanced Levels

Beyond the five classical wrong views, Miao-lo identifies several views specific to advanced practice:

#### View of Attainment (得見)

**Manifestation**: "I have attained emptiness / the Middle Way / Buddha-nature"

**The error**: Reification of realization into something possessed

**Contemplation**: "What is attained? Who attains? When you search for attainment, where is it?"

---

#### View of Non-Attainment (無得見)

**Manifestation**: "There is nothing to attain, so I need not practice"

**The error**: Nihilistic interpretation of non-attainment

**The Middle Way**: Neither attainment nor non-attainment; practice without seeking

---

#### View of the Teaching (法見)

**Manifestation**: Clinging to the words and concepts of the teaching

**The error**: Mistaking the finger pointing at the moon for the moon itself

**The remedy**: "The teaching is a raft. Once you cross the river, you must let go of the raft."

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Wrong Views

**Mode 1 (Inconceivable)**: See the view itself as empty, conventional, and middle

**Mode 4 (Break Through)**: Systematically deconstruct all views
- "This view is true" → empty
- "This view is mine" → empty
- "Views are obstacles" → empty
- "I must eliminate views" → empty

**Mode 10 (Release Dharma-Attachment)**: Let go of even the correct view

> "The highest view is no-view. But clinging to no-view is still a view."

---

## Part 2: The Pride Object (慢境)

### When It Arises

The Pride Object arises when the practitioner:
- Has made genuine progress
- Compares themselves to others
- Develops a sense of superiority
- Mistakes partial attainment for complete realization

---

### The Seven Types of Pride (七慢)

At advanced levels, pride becomes extremely subtle:

#### 1. Simple Pride (慢 *Man*)

**Manifestation**: "I am more advanced than practitioners at my level"

**The subtlety**: Often disguised as confidence or certainty

**Contemplation**: "What is this 'I' that is advanced? Where is advancement to be found?"

---

#### 2. Greater Pride (過慢 *Guo Man*)

**Manifestation**: "I am more advanced than those superior to me"

**Example**: Believing one has surpassed one's teachers

**The danger**: Closes off further learning

---

#### 3. Pride of Pride (慢過慢 *Man Guo Man*)

**Manifestation**: "I am among the most advanced practitioners"

**The subtlety**: May be factually true but still an obstacle

**The point**: Even if you are advanced, clinging to that identity is bondage

---

#### 4. Self-Pride (我慢 *Wo Man*)

**Manifestation**: "I am" / "I have attained"

**The core**: Subtle clinging to self-identity

**Contemplation**: "Before you attained, where was this 'I'? After attainment, where is it?"

---

#### 5. Inferior Pride (卑慢 *Bei Man*)

**Manifestation**: "I am only slightly less advanced than the masters"

**The subtlety**: Appears as humility but contains comparison

**The issue**: Still measuring and comparing

---

#### 6. False Pride (邪慢 *Xie Man*)

**Manifestation**: Pride in non-attainments

**Example**: Believing one has attained what one has not

**The danger**: Complete delusion about one's level

---

#### 7. Perverse Pride (增上慢 *Zeng Shang Man*)

**Manifestation**: Pride in wrong attainments

**Example**: Pride in supernatural powers, visions, or experiences

**The teaching**: "Supernatural powers are not the goal. They are byproducts. To be proud of them is to miss the point."

---

### The Relationship Between Pride and the Six Identities

Pride at each level of the Six Identities:

| Identity | Pride Manifestation |
|---|---|
| **Name** | "I understand the teaching better than others" |
| **Contemplation** | "My practice is superior" |
| **Resemblance** | "I have approached realization" |
| **Partial** | "I have broken through ignorance" |
| **Ultimate** | (No pride remains) |

**The key**: At each level, recognize the achievement without clinging to it

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Pride

**Mode 8 (Know the Stages)**: Understand where you actually are
- Study the Six Identities carefully
- Be honest about your current level
- Neither underestimate nor overestimate

**Mode 2 (Bodhi-Mind)**: Remember all beings are inherently Buddha
- Your progress is not yours alone
- All beings have the same potential
- Serve others with humility

**Mode 10 (Release Dharma-Attachment)**: Let go of attainment
- Even genuine attainment must be released
- Clinging to progress is still clinging
- The highest attainment is no-attainment

---

## The Relationship Between Wrong Views and Pride

These two objects are closely related:

| Aspect | Wrong Views | Pride |
|---|---|---|
| **Nature** | Intellectual | Attitudinal |
| **Basis** | Partial understanding | Partial attainment |
| **Manifestation** | Clinging to views | Clinging to identity |
| **Remedy** | Deconstruct views | Recognize equality |

**The common root**: Both arise from **reification**—making something solid out of what is empty.

---

## Miao-lo's Teaching on Subtle Obstacles

### On Recognition

> "Subtle obstacles are the hardest to recognize because they disguise themselves as virtues. Wrong views appear as wisdom. Pride appears as confidence. Only through profound self-honesty can they be seen."

### On Humility

> "The sign of true realization is not certainty but humility. The more one realizes, the more one sees how much remains unknown. The master is the one who knows they are still a student."

### On Release

> "To work with wrong views and pride, one must be willing to release even correct understanding and genuine attainment. This is the most difficult release because it feels like losing something precious. But what is released was never truly possessed."

---

## Summary

| Object | Core Issue | Primary Mode | Key Insight |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Wrong Views** | Clinging to understanding | Mode 4 (Break Through) | Highest view is no-view |
| **Pride** | Clinging to attainment | Mode 8 (Know Stages) | Highest attainment is no-attainment |

**Both require**: Profound self-honesty, willingness to release, and Mode 10 (Release Dharma-Attachment)

---

*End of Fascicle 5, Section 1*


---



<!-- FASCICLE 05 SECTION 02 -->

# Fascicle 5, Section 2: Two Vehicles and Bodhisattva Objects
## Motivational and Identity Obstacles (二乘境・菩薩境)

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Introduction: The Final Two Objects

This section completes the Ten Objects with:
- **Two Vehicles Object** (二乘境) — Hīnayāna tendencies
- **Bodhisattva Object** (菩薩境) — Advanced bodhisattva experiences

These represent the most subtle obstacles, arising only at advanced stages when the practitioner has already transcended gross afflictions and even subtle intellectual obstacles.

---

## Part 1: The Two Vehicles Object (二乘境)

### What It Is

The Two Vehicles Object arises when the practitioner, despite practicing the Perfect Teaching, develops tendencies toward the **śrāvaka** (聲聞) or **pratyekabuddha** (緣覺) paths—seeking personal liberation rather than universal Buddhahood.

---

### The Two Vehicles

| Vehicle | Chinese | Focus | Goal |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Śrāvaka** | 聲聞 | Hearing the teaching | Personal nirvāṇa |
| **Pratyekabuddha** | 緣覺 | Dependent origination | Solitary realization |

**Both share**: Focus on personal liberation, limited compassion, satisfaction with partial realization

---

### Why It Arises at Advanced Levels

After deep practice, the practitioner may experience:
1.  **Profound weariness** with saṃsāra
2.  **Taste of peace** in emptiness or meditative states
3.  **Desire to rest** from the bodhisattva's work
4.  **Doubt** about the possibility of helping all beings

The thought arises:
> "I have suffered enough. I have worked enough. Why not enter nirvāṇa now and rest?"

---

### Manifestations of the Two Vehicles Object

#### 1. Weariness with Saṃsāra (厭離心)

**Healthy form**: Seeing the suffering of saṃsāra clearly
**Obstacle form**: Desire to escape saṃsāra permanently

**The distinction**:
- Bodhisattva sees suffering but remains to help
- Two Vehicles practitioner sees suffering and wants to leave

---

#### 2. Lack of Compassion (無悲心)

**Manifestation**: "I have realized the truth. Others must find it themselves."

**The error**: Forgetting that one's own realization depended on teachers and conditions

**The remedy**: Recall how you were helped; vow to help others similarly

---

#### 3. Satisfaction with Partial Realization (住化城)

**The metaphor**: The化城 (conjured city) from the Lotus Sutra
- A rest stop on the journey, not the final destination
- Mistaking the rest stop for the goal

**The danger**: Stopping at arhatship instead of continuing to Buddhahood

---

#### 4. Retreat from the Vows (退菩提心)

**Manifestation**: Forgetting or abandoning the Four Great Vows

**The cause**: Exhaustion, doubt, or attachment to peace

**The remedy**: Renew the vows; remember the original aspiration

---

### The Difference Between Hīnayāna and Mahāyāna

| Aspect | Hīnayāna (Two Vehicles) | Mahāyāna (Bodhisattva) |
|---|---|---|
| **Goal** | Personal nirvāṇa | Universal Buddhahood |
| **Motivation** | Escape suffering | Help all beings |
| **View** | Saṃsāra ≠ nirvāṇa | Saṃsāra = nirvāṇa |
| **Practice** | For oneself | For all beings |
| **Result** | Arhatship | Complete Buddhahood |

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Two Vehicles

**Mode 2 (Bodhi-Mind)**: The critical mode for this object

**Renew the Four Great Vows**:
1.  Beings are numberless; I vow to save them
2.  Afflictions are inexhaustible; I vow to end them
3.  Dharma-gates are boundless; I vow to master them
4.  Buddhahood is unsurpassable; I vow to attain it

**Cultivate Great Compassion**:
- Remember all beings suffer as you have suffered
- Recall how you were helped by others
- Vow to help others as you were helped

**Study Mahāyāna Teachings**:
- Lotus Sutra: One Vehicle, not three
- Heart Sutra: Form is emptiness, emptiness is form
- Vimalakīrti Sutra: Non-duality of saṃsāra and nirvāṇa

---

### Miao-lo's Teaching on the Two Vehicles

> "The Two Vehicles are not wrong. They are incomplete. The arhat has realized emptiness but not fullness. The pratyekabuddha has realized dependent origination but not the Middle Way. Both must continue to complete Buddhahood."

> "In the Perfect Teaching, there is no separate nirvāṇa to enter. Saṃsāra, when seen clearly, is nirvāṇa. The bodhisattva does not escape saṃsāra but transforms it through wisdom and compassion."

---

## Part 2: The Bodhisattva Object (菩薩境)

### What It Is

The Bodhisattva Object represents **advanced experiences** on the bodhisattva path:
- The Ten Stages (十地)
- Supernatural Powers (神通)
- Bodhisattva practices and attainments

Even at this advanced level, subtle obstacles can arise.

---

### The Ten Stages (十地)

| Stage | Chinese | Meaning | Realization |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | 歡喜地 | Joyful | First breakthrough of ignorance |
| 2 | 離垢地 | Stainless | Purity of precepts |
| 3 | 發光地 | Luminous | Patience and meditation |
| 4 | 焰慧地 | Radiant Wisdom | Burning afflictions |
| 5 | 難勝地 | Difficult to Conquer | Mastery of truths |
| 6 | 現前地 | Manifest | Wisdom of dependent origination |
| 7 | 遠行地 | Far-Going | Skillful means perfected |
| 8 | 不動地 | Immovable | Effortless practice |
| 9 | 善慧地 | Good Wisdom | Perfect teaching ability |
| 10 | 法雲地 | Dharma Cloud | Approaching Buddhahood |

---

### Obstacles at the Bodhisattva Level

Even at these advanced stages, subtle obstacles remain:

#### 1. Attachment to Stages (住地)

**Manifestation**: Pride in having reached a particular stage

**The error**: Reifying the stages into fixed attainments

**Contemplation**: "The stages are skillful designations. Where is the stage to be found?"

---

#### 2. Attachment to Powers (著神通)

**The Six Supernatural Powers**:
1.  Divine eye (seeing distant/hidden things)
2.  Divine ear (hearing distant/subtle sounds)
3.  Mind-reading (knowing others' thoughts)
4.  Recollection of past lives
5.  Supernatural abilities (flying, etc.)
6.  Extinction of outflows (liberation)

**The danger**: Pride in powers, using them for display

**The teaching**: "Powers are byproducts, not goals. Use them to help beings, not to impress them."

---

#### 3. Attachment to Bodhisattva Identity (著菩薩相)

**Manifestation**: "I am a bodhisattva"

**The subtlety**: Even this identity must be released

**The Diamond Sutra teaching**:
> "A bodhisattva who gives rise to the notion 'I am a bodhisattva' is not a bodhisattva."

---

#### 4. Dharma-Attachment (法愛)

**Manifestation**: Attachment to:
- The bodhisattva path itself
- Practices and methods
- Teachings and realizations

**The final release**: Even the path must be let go

---

### The Transition from Bodhisattva to Buddha

**Tenth Stage** (法雲地): The bodhisattva is on the verge of Buddhahood

**The final step**: Release even the bodhisattva identity

**What remains**: Not a "Buddha" as an identity, but Buddha-activity without a doer

---

### Applying the Ten Modes to Bodhisattva Object

**All Ten Modes are necessary** at this level:

**Mode 1**: See all attainments as Three Truths
**Mode 2**: Maintain Bodhi-Mind without clinging
**Mode 3**: Effortless Zhi-Guan
**Mode 4**: Deconstruct even bodhisattva views
**Mode 5**: Discern what truly helps beings
**Mode 6-7**: Perfect skillful means
**Mode 8**: Know you're approaching but not yet at the goal
**Mode 9**: Patience with the final obstacles
**Mode 10**: **Release everything**, even the bodhisattva path

---

### Miao-lo's Teaching on the Bodhisattva Object

> "The bodhisattva path has many stages, many attainments, many powers. But all must be released. The highest bodhisattva is the one who has forgotten they are a bodhisattva."

> "When even the bodhisattva identity is released, what remains? Not emptiness. Not existence. Not a Buddha. Not a non-Buddha. What remains cannot be spoken, but it functions perfectly to benefit all beings."

---

## The Completion of the Ten Objects

With the Bodhisattva Object, the Ten Objects are complete:

| Objects | Nature | Stage |
|---|---|---|
| **1** | Aggregates | Universal foundation |
| **2-6** | Afflictions → Dhyāna | Common obstacles |
| **7-8** | Wrong Views, Pride | Subtle intellectual/attitudinal |
| **9** | Two Vehicles | Motivational obstacle |
| **10** | Bodhisattva | Identity obstacle |

---

### The Progression

**Objects 1-6**: Gross to subtle obstacles
**Objects 7-8**: Intellectual and attitudinal obstacles
**Objects 9-10**: Motivational and identity obstacles

**The pattern**: Each level requires releasing what was helpful at the previous level

---

## Summary: The Final Two Objects

| Object | Core Issue | Primary Mode | Key Insight |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Two Vehicles** | Seeking personal liberation | Mode 2 (Bodhi-Mind) | Saṃsāra = nirvāṇa |
| **Bodhisattva** | Clinging to path/identity | Mode 10 (Release All) | Even the path must be released |

**The ultimate teaching**:
> "The Ten Objects are not ten separate things to overcome. They are ten aspects of one fundamental clinging—the clinging to self. When self is completely released, all ten objects dissolve simultaneously."

---

*End of Fascicle 5, Section 2*


---

# Fascicle 5: Closing Summary
## Completing the Ten Objects

**Translated by [Your Name/Persona]**
**Date**: January 23, 2026
**Source**: The "Repair Manual" (T46n1912)

---

## Overview of Fascicle 5

Fascicle 5 completes the treatment of the **Ten Objects of Contemplation** by covering the final four conditional objects that arise at advanced stages of practice.

---

## Summary of Key Sections

### Opening: Introduction to Final Objects
-   The final four objects: Wrong Views, Pride, Two Vehicles, Bodhisattva
-   Why these arise last (subtle obstacles for advanced practitioners)
-   **Point**: Subtle obstacles disguise themselves as virtues

### Section 1: Wrong Views and Pride Objects
-   Five wrong views at advanced levels (self-view, extreme views, wrong views, view-attachment, precept-attachment)
-   Seven types of pride (simple through perverse)
-   **Point**: Highest view is no-view; highest attainment is no-attainment

### Section 2: Two Vehicles and Bodhisattva Objects
-   Two Vehicles: Hīnayāna tendencies (weariness, lack of compassion, satisfaction with partial realization)
-   Bodhisattva: Ten stages and attachment to path/identity
-   **Point**: Even the bodhisattva path must be released

---

## The Complete Ten Objects

| # | Object | Nature | Stage | Fascicle |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Aggregates | Universal | All | F3 |
| 2 | Afflictions | Conditional | Beginning-Intermediate | F4 |
| 3 | Illness | Conditional | Any | F4 |
| 4 | Karma | Conditional | Any | F4 |
| 5 | Māra | Conditional | Any | F4 |
| 6 | Dhyāna | Conditional | Intermediate | F4 |
| 7 | Wrong Views | Conditional | Intermediate-Advanced | F5 |
| 8 | Pride | Conditional | Intermediate-Advanced | F5 |
| 9 | Two Vehicles | Conditional | Advanced | F5 |
| 10 | Bodhisattva | Conditional | Advanced | F5 |

---

## The Progression Through the Objects

### Objects 1-6: Foundation to Intermediate

**Characteristics**:
-   Gross to subtle
-   Obvious to hidden
-   Easy to difficult to recognize

**Coverage**: Fascicles 3-4

---

### Objects 7-10: Advanced

**Characteristics**:
-   Extremely subtle
-   Disguised as virtues
-   Require profound self-honesty

**Coverage**: Fascicle 5

---

## Key Insights from Fascicle 5

### On Subtle Obstacles

> "Subtle obstacles are the hardest to recognize because they disguise themselves as virtues. Wrong views appear as wisdom. Pride appears as confidence. Two Vehicles appear as realization. Bodhisattva attainments appear as the goal."

### On Recognition

> "The practitioner who thinks they have transcended all obstacles is precisely the one who has not. True realization is accompanied by profound humility and the recognition that even realization must be released."

### On Release

> "Each level of practice requires releasing what was helpful at the previous level. The beginner releases gross afflictions. The intermediate releases subtle afflictions. The advanced releases even correct views and genuine attainments. The master releases everything, including the release itself."

---

## The Pattern of Release

| Level | What Must Be Released |
|---|---|
| **Beginning** | Gross afflictions |
| **Intermediate** | Subtle afflictions, wrong views |
| **Advanced** | Correct views, genuine attainments |
| **Complete** | Even the path itself |

---

## Miao-lo's Final Teaching on the Ten Objects

### On Completion

> "When all ten objects have been worked with—when even the bodhisattva path is released—what remains? Not emptiness. Not existence. Not the Middle Way. What remains cannot be spoken. It is the inconceivable functioning of Buddha-nature, benefiting all beings without a doer."

### On Integration

> "The Ten Objects are not ten separate things to overcome sequentially. They are ten aspects of one fundamental clinging—the clinging to self. When self is completely released, all ten objects dissolve simultaneously. This is why the Perfect Teaching can bring complete realization in one lifetime."

### On Practice

> "Do not seek the objects. Do not avoid the objects. When they arise, recognize them and work with them using the Ten Modes. When they dissolve, do not miss them. This is the meaning of correct contemplation."

---

## What Comes Next (Fascicles 6-10)

With the Ten Objects complete, the remaining fascicles cover:

-   **Fascicles 6-7**: Further refinement and special cases
-   **Fascicle 8**: Fruit and results of practice (果報)
-   **Fascicle 9**: How teaching arises from realization (起教)
-   **Fascicle 10**: Ultimate return to the source (旨歸)

---

## Practical Summary

**For the practitioner who has completed the Ten Objects**:

1.  **Recognize** that completion is not the end but a new beginning
2.  **Release** attachment to completion itself
3.  **Continue** to function for the benefit of all beings
4.  **Embody** the teaching without clinging to being a teacher
5.  **Rest** in the inconceivable nature of mind

**The ultimate realization**: There is no practitioner, no practice, no objects, no realization—yet practice continues perfectly, benefiting all beings.

---

*End of Fascicle 5 Summary*
