<!-- FASCICLE 08 SECTION 02 -->

# Fascicle 8: Section 2 — The Illness Object (病患境)
## Scholarly Translation

**Source**: T46n1912, Fascicle 8, Parts 2-3 (卷第八之二、之三)
**Author**: Miao-lo (Zhanran, 湛然, 711-782 CE)
**Translator**: William Altig / Claude
**Date**: January 23, 2026

**Five Flavors Assessment**: Ghee (法華涅槃) — Illness as dharma-gate
**Six Stages Location**: Practice (修行即) — Active processing of source material

---

## Object 3: The Illness Object (病患境)

### I. Introduction: Illness as Contemplative Phenomenon

The third of the Ten Objects addresses physical illness (病患) that arises during meditation practice. Unlike the Affliction Object, which deals with mental disturbances, the Illness Object concerns the body itself.

> 次明病患。病起多途。

"Next, we clarify illness. Illness arises through many channels."

Miao-lo immediately signals that illness is not a single phenomenon but manifests through diverse causes, each requiring distinct recognition and treatment.

### II. The Six Causes of Illness

Miao-lo identifies six primary causes of illness arising during practice:

#### A. Four Elements Imbalance (四大不調)

> 四大不調故病

"Illness due to the four great elements being out of balance."

The body is constituted of earth (地), water (水), fire (火), and wind (風). When these fall out of proportion, illness results:

| Element | Excess Produces | Deficiency Produces |
|---------|-----------------|---------------------|
| Earth (地) | Heaviness, tumors | Weakness, emaciation |
| Water (水) | Swelling, phlegm | Dryness, fever |
| Fire (火) | Fever, inflammation | Coldness, poor digestion |
| Wind (風) | Trembling, pain | Stiffness, paralysis |

> 地大增者。肢節沈重。水大增者。涕唾流溢。火大增者。身熱燋燥。風大增者。氣息喘急。

"When earth increases, the limbs become heavy. When water increases, mucus and saliva overflow. When fire increases, the body becomes hot and parched. When wind increases, the breath becomes labored."

#### B. Improper Diet (飲食不節)

> 飲食不節故病

"Illness due to immoderate eating and drinking."

This includes:
- Eating too much or too little
- Eating at improper times
- Eating incompatible foods together
- Eating impure or unsuitable foods

The *Śikṣāsamuccaya* similarly emphasizes that food should be taken "not for beauty or strength, but merely to sustain the body for the practice of the Path."

#### C. Meditation Imbalance (坐禪不調)

> 坐禪不調故病

"Illness due to imbalanced sitting meditation."

This is particularly relevant to contemplatives. Meditation itself can cause illness when:

1. **Posture errors**: Sitting incorrectly strains the body
2. **Breath control errors**: Forcing the breath disrupts the wind element
3. **Mental forcing**: Excessive striving creates tension
4. **Timing errors**: Meditating when exhausted or ill

> 若坐禪時不善調和。身中四大互相乖越。則病發生。

"If during seated meditation one does not skillfully harmonize, the four elements in the body mutually transgress each other, and illness arises."

#### D. Karmic Manifestation (業報所感)

> 業報所感故病

"Illness due to the manifestation of karmic retribution."

Some illnesses arise not from present causes but from past karma ripening in the present:

> 過去惡業今生受報。故生重病。

"Evil karma from past lives is now being experienced as retribution. Therefore heavy illness arises."

This type of illness may not respond to medical treatment or contemplative adjustment because its root lies in the karmic storehouse.

#### E. Demonic Interference (鬼神所作)

> 鬼神所作故病

"Illness caused by ghosts and spirits."

External non-human entities may afflict the body:

> 若有魔鬼附著其身。則病苦發。

"If demonic ghosts attach to the body, illness and suffering arise."

This requires different treatment methods—specifically, the protective practices (護持) and dharani recitation discussed in the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*.

#### F. Contemplative Rebound (觀行逆發)

> 觀行力故舊業發動

"Due to the power of contemplative practice, old karma is activated."

This is distinctive to practitioners. Intensive contemplation can accelerate karmic maturation, causing latent diseases to manifest prematurely:

> 由功行故。宿業遂發。而為疾患。

"Due to meritorious practice, latent karma is activated and becomes illness."

This is sometimes called "purification through practice"—the body processes old karma more rapidly because of contemplative intensity.

### III. The 101 Illnesses

Miao-lo references the traditional classification of 101 diseases:

> 一大不調有百一病。四大不調有四百四病。

"When one great element is out of balance, there are 101 illnesses. When all four great elements are out of balance, there are 404 illnesses."

This derives from Indian medical theory transmitted through Buddhist texts:

| Category | Number | Total |
|----------|--------|-------|
| Earth imbalance | 101 | 101 |
| Water imbalance | 101 | 101 |
| Fire imbalance | 101 | 101 |
| Wind imbalance | 101 | 101 |
| **Total** | — | **404** |

### IV. Six Treatment Methods

Miao-lo presents six methods for treating illness that arises during practice:

#### Method 1: Breath Regulation (止息)

> 若因坐禪氣息不調而發病者。當善調息。

"If illness arises during seated meditation due to imbalanced breath, one should skillfully regulate the breath."

This includes the **Six Healing Breaths** (六氣):

| Breath | Sound | Function | Element |
|--------|-------|----------|---------|
| 吹 (chuī) | "blowing" | Cools heat | Fire excess |
| 呼 (hū) | "exhaling" | Expels blockage | Earth excess |
| 嘻 (xī) | "sighing" | Disperses wind | Wind excess |
| 呵 (hē) | "ha" | Releases heart-fire | Fire/heart |
| 噓 (xū) | "shh" | Calms liver | Wood/liver |
| 呬 (sì) | "ss" | Clears lungs | Metal/lung |

#### Method 2: Mental Adjustment (假想)

> 若四大不調而發病者。當作假想觀。

"If illness arises due to four-element imbalance, one should practice imaginative contemplation."

This involves visualizing the elements coming into balance:

> 想諸氣息流入百脈。隨意周遍。想冷想暖。隨病所宜。

"Imagine the various breaths flowing into the hundred channels, pervading throughout as desired. Imagine cold or warmth according to what the illness requires."

#### Method 3: Twelve Breath Techniques (十二息)

Miao-lo lists twelve types of breath manipulation:

1. 上息 (ascending breath)
2. 下息 (descending breath)
3. 滿息 (filling breath)
4. 燋息 (parching breath)
5. 增長息 (increasing breath)
6. 滅壞息 (destroying breath)
7. 暖息 (warming breath)
8. 冷息 (cooling breath)
9. 衝息 (rushing breath)
10. 持息 (holding breath)
11. 和息 (harmonizing breath)
12. 補息 (supplementing breath)

> 此十二種息。治四百四病。隨病所宜。善巧用之。

"These twelve kinds of breath treat the 404 illnesses. According to what each illness requires, use them skillfully."

#### Method 4: Mental Stabilization (安心)

> 若病由心生。當安心觀法。

"If illness arises from the mind, one should stabilize the mind and contemplate dharma."

This addresses psychosomatic illness—conditions generated by mental states affecting the body:

> 攀緣憂畏故發病者。當安心不動。

"If illness arises from grasping, worry, and fear, one should stabilize the mind without movement."

#### Method 5: Medical Treatment (服藥)

> 若四大病甚。非觀行所治者。當服諸藥。

"If the four-element illness is severe and not treatable by contemplative practice, one should take medicines."

Miao-lo acknowledges that contemplation cannot treat all illnesses. Some require external intervention:

> 隨病服藥。不著於味。

"Take medicine according to the illness without attachment to its taste."

This aligns with the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s instruction that medicine should be taken "without greed or attachment to taste."

#### Method 6: Mantras and Protective Practices (持呪)

> 若鬼神病。當誦呪術。

"If the illness is from ghosts and spirits, one should recite mantras."

For illness caused by external entities:

> 誦持神呪。存念三寶。

"Recite and maintain divine mantras. Be mindful of the Three Treasures."

### V. Applying the Ten Modes to Illness

Miao-lo demonstrates how each of the Ten Modes applies to the Illness Object:

#### Mode 1: Contemplating the Inconceivable Object (觀不思議境)

> 觀病即法界。四大即三諦。

"Contemplate that illness is precisely the dharma-realm. The four great elements are precisely the three truths."

The illness is not separate from reality; it manifests the three truths:

- **Empty**: The illness has no inherent existence
- **Provisional**: It functions as a temporary condition
- **Middle**: It integrates both aspects simultaneously

#### Mode 2: Arousing the Bodhi-Mind (發菩提心)

> 因病發心。眾生有病我亦有病。同體大悲。

"Because of illness, generate the [bodhi-]mind. When sentient beings are ill, I too am ill. This is great compassion of the same essence."

The practitioner's own illness becomes a gateway to compassion for all who suffer illness throughout the dharma-realm.

#### Mode 3: Skillfully Settling the Mind (善巧安心)

> 安心於病。不生厭離。不生貪著。

"Settle the mind upon illness. Generate neither aversion nor attachment."

The practitioner neither rejects the illness with disgust nor grasps at it with fascination, but settles the mind in equanimity.

#### Modes 4-10: Complete Application

The remaining modes are applied similarly:

- **Mode 4** (破法遍): Break through the characteristics of illness
- **Mode 5** (識通塞): Discern when illness obstructs or opens the path
- **Mode 6** (調道品): Adjust the path-factors to accommodate illness
- **Mode 7** (助道對治): Apply aids and antidotes appropriate to illness
- **Mode 8** (識次位): Recognize one's stage relative to illness
- **Mode 9** (能安忍): Endure illness with patience
- **Mode 10** (無法愛): Avoid attachment to states achieved during illness

### VI. The Body as Contemplative Object

The *Śikṣāsamuccaya* describes the body as a collection of impurities—"a sack of grain" filled with various substances, "a residence of eighty thousand families of worms." Miao-lo incorporates this perspective:

> 觀身不淨。四大假合。

"Contemplate the body as impure. The four great elements are provisionally combined."

Yet the Tiantai approach integrates this with the understanding that the body is also the vehicle of practice:

> 借假修真。不棄此身。

"Borrow the provisional to cultivate the real. Do not abandon this body."

The body—with all its illnesses—becomes the very medium through which realization occurs.

### VII. Cognitive Deconstruction of Illness

Following the emptiness teaching, Miao-lo applies analytical deconstruction:

> 病從何來。病往何去。中間誰病。

"Where does illness come from? Where does illness go? Who is ill in between?"

This corresponds to the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s analysis: "By analyzing the elements, one realizes there is no 'self,' 'being,' or 'living soul' that is actually sick or suffering; there are only the elements and conditions interacting."

> 尋病不可得。即是病性空。

"Searching for illness, it cannot be found. This is precisely the empty nature of illness."

### VIII. Doctrinal Significance

The Illness Object (病患境) establishes that physical conditions arising during practice are not impediments but objects of contemplation themselves. Miao-lo presents a graduated approach:

1. **Recognize the cause**: Identify which of the six causes applies
2. **Apply appropriate treatment**: Match method to cause
3. **Contemplate the nature**: Perceive illness as empty, provisional, and middle
4. **Transform into path**: Use illness as gateway to compassion and wisdom

This differs from approaches that view illness as purely negative:

> 善知識能轉病為道。

"Good teachers can transform illness into the path."

The practitioner who becomes ill during contemplation has not failed—they have encountered another object requiring the application of the Ten Modes.

---

## Key Technical Terms

| Chinese | Pinyin | Definition |
|---------|--------|------------|
| 病患境 | bìng huàn jìng | Illness Object |
| 四大不調 | sì dà bù tiáo | Four elements imbalance |
| 飲食不節 | yǐn shí bù jié | Immoderate eating |
| 坐禪不調 | zuò chán bù tiáo | Meditation imbalance |
| 業報所感 | yè bào suǒ gǎn | Karmic manifestation |
| 鬼神所作 | guǐ shén suǒ zuò | Caused by spirits |
| 六氣 | liù qì | Six healing breaths |
| 十二息 | shí èr xī | Twelve breath techniques |
| 四百四病 | sì bǎi sì bìng | 404 illnesses |
| 假想觀 | jiǎ xiǎng guān | Imaginative contemplation |
| 安心觀法 | ān xīn guān fǎ | Stabilizing mind, contemplating dharma |

---

## Cross-References

- **Indian Sources**: Treatment methods align with *Śikṣāsamuccaya* Ch. 6 (Ātmabhāvarakṣā) on protecting the body-self and Ch. 14 (Ātmabhāvapariśuddhi) on purifying the body
- **Chinese Medical Context**: The six breaths and twelve breath techniques derive from Chinese medical-Daoist tradition integrated into Buddhist practice
- **Tiantai Context**: This section presupposes the framework of Objects 1-2 and the Ten Modes from Fascicles 5-7

---

**END OF SECTION 2**



---



<!-- FASCICLE 08 SECTION 03 -->

# Fascicle 8: Section 3 — The Karma Object (業境)
## Scholarly Translation

**Source**: T46n1912, Fascicle 8, Part 3 (卷第八之三)
**Author**: Miao-lo (Zhanran, 湛然, 711-782 CE)
**Translator**: William Altig / Claude
**Date**: January 23, 2026

**Five Flavors Assessment**: Ghee (法華涅槃) — Karma as gateway to liberation
**Six Stages Location**: Practice (修行即) — Active processing of source material

---

## Object 4: The Karma Object (業境)

### I. Introduction: Karma as Contemplative Phenomenon

The fourth of the Ten Objects addresses karma (業) that arises during contemplation. Unlike the Affliction Object (mental disturbance) and Illness Object (physical condition), the Karma Object concerns the manifestation of past actions as visions, signs, and obstacles during meditation.

> 次明業境。業是過去所造。今因禪觀而發。

"Next, we clarify the karma object. Karma is what was created in the past. Now, because of meditative contemplation, it arises."

Miao-lo identifies a distinctive phenomenon: intensive practice can accelerate the manifestation of latent karma, causing past actions to appear as present experiences during meditation.

### II. The Nature of Karmic Manifestation

#### A. How Karma Arises During Practice

> 由觀行力故。宿世惡業忽然現前。

"Due to the power of contemplative practice, evil karma from past lives suddenly manifests in the present."

This occurs through several mechanisms:

1. **Contemplative acceleration**: Deep practice speeds karmic ripening
2. **Mental purification**: As obscurations thin, latent karma becomes visible
3. **Karmic pressure**: Accumulated karma seeks expression

> 如風吹土。塵埃忽起。非風造塵。塵本在土。

"Like wind blowing earth, dust suddenly rises. The wind does not create the dust; the dust was already in the earth."

Miao-lo's metaphor clarifies that practice does not create karma but reveals what was already present.

#### B. Forms of Karmic Manifestation

Karma manifests in several ways during meditation:

| Manifestation | Chinese | Description |
|---------------|---------|-------------|
| Visions | 見業相 | Past actions appear as mental images |
| Physical sensations | 身業發 | Bodily symptoms tied to past karma |
| Emotional surges | 心業發 | Sudden waves of guilt, fear, or remorse |
| Dream signs | 夢中業相 | Karmic content in dreams |

### III. The Classification of Karmic Signs (業相)

Miao-lo systematizes the signs that indicate karmic manifestation:

#### A. Signs of Unwholesome Karma (不善業相)

> 若見地獄餓鬼畜生等相。當知是過去不善業發。

"If one sees signs of hell, hungry ghosts, or animals, know that this is past unwholesome karma arising."

| Vision | Indicates | Past Cause |
|--------|-----------|------------|
| Hell realms | Heavy negative karma | Killing, hatred |
| Hungry ghost realms | Moderate negative karma | Greed, stinginess |
| Animal realms | Delusion-based karma | Ignorance, stupidity |
| Asura realms | Contentious karma | Jealousy, fighting |

This corresponds to the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s teaching on visualizing karmic results—specific past actions manifest as "grotesque forms" during contemplation.

#### B. Signs of Wholesome Karma (善業相)

> 若見天宮人道淨土等相。當知是過去善業發。

"If one sees heavenly palaces, human realms, or pure lands, know that this is past wholesome karma arising."

Even positive karmic signs require attention—they can generate attachment and pride.

#### C. Signs of Purification (淨業相)

The *Śikṣāsamuccaya* provides specific purification signs that appear in dreams:

- Vomiting bad food (expelling negativity)
- Eating yogurt or milk (receiving pure nourishment)
- Seeing sun or moon (illumination)
- Moving through sky (transcendence)
- Defeating dark figures (overcoming Māra/death)
- Seeing monastic assembly (connection to Sangha)
- Climbing trees or mountains (spiritual ascent)

> 夢中見斬頭。是煩惱盡相。

"Dreaming of beheading indicates the exhaustion of afflictions."

### IV. The Three Types of Karma

Miao-lo classifies karma according to its weight and treatability:

#### A. Fixed Karma (定業)

> 定業者。重業必受果報。

"Fixed karma: heavy karma that must receive its retribution."

This includes the five heinous acts (五逆):
1. Killing one's father
2. Killing one's mother
3. Killing an arhat
4. Shedding the blood of a Buddha
5. Creating schism in the Sangha

#### B. Unfixed Karma (不定業)

> 不定業者。輕業可轉。

"Unfixed karma: light karma that can be transformed."

This karma is susceptible to change through practice, repentance, and contemplation.

#### C. Present-Life Karma (現業)

> 現業者。今生所造。

"Present-life karma: what is created in this lifetime."

This is still being formed and can be redirected before it ripens.

### V. The Four Powers of Purification

Miao-lo draws on the traditional four powers (四力) for working with karma, corresponding to the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s *Caturdharmaka Sūtra* teaching:

#### Power 1: Revulsion (追悔力)

> 追悔力者。於所造罪深生慚愧。

"The power of revulsion: regarding the created sins, generate deep shame and remorse."

This involves acknowledging specific past actions without rationalization or denial.

#### Power 2: Antidote (對治力)

> 對治力者。修諸善法以滅惡業。

"The power of the antidote: cultivate various wholesome dharmas to extinguish evil karma."

Specific antidotes include:
- Studying profound sutras
- Meditating on emptiness
- Reciting mantras
- Erecting Buddha images
- Offering at stupas

#### Power 3: Restraint (遮止力)

> 遮止力者。誓願更不復作。

"The power of restraint: vow never to repeat the action."

This is the binding commitment to abstain from future negative actions.

#### Power 4: Support (依止力)

> 依止力者。歸依三寶發菩提心。

"The power of support: take refuge in the Three Treasures and generate bodhicitta."

The *Śikṣāsamuccaya* compares bodhicitta to "the fire at the end of an aeon, capable of consuming enormous amounts of past negative karma."

### VI. Applying the Ten Modes to Karma

Miao-lo demonstrates how each of the Ten Modes applies to the Karma Object:

#### Mode 1: Contemplating the Inconceivable Object (觀不思議境)

> 觀業即法界。業性本空。

"Contemplate that karma is precisely the dharma-realm. The nature of karma is fundamentally empty."

The karma is not separate from reality; it manifests the three truths:

- **Empty**: Karma has no inherent existence; no "doer" can be found
- **Provisional**: It functions according to causes and conditions
- **Middle**: It integrates both aspects simultaneously

> 業如夢幻。雖有作用。而無實體。

"Karma is like a dream or illusion. Although it has function, it has no real substance."

This corresponds to the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s teaching: "While karma and its ripening function, no intrinsic 'thing' moves from this life to the next."

#### Mode 2: Arousing the Bodhi-Mind (發菩提心)

> 因業發心。我及眾生皆有如是業障。願皆解脫。

"Because of karma, generate the [bodhi-]mind. Both I and all sentient beings have such karmic obstacles. May all be liberated."

The practitioner's own karmic manifestations become a gateway to universal compassion.

#### Mode 3: Skillfully Settling the Mind (善巧安心)

> 安心於業相。不驚不怖。不喜不憂。

"Settle the mind upon karmic signs. Neither startled nor frightened, neither pleased nor worried."

The practitioner maintains equanimity whether positive or negative karma manifests.

#### Mode 4: Breaking Through All Dharmas (破法遍)

> 破業相空。無業可得。

"Break through karmic characteristics to emptiness. No karma can be found."

This applies the analytical deconstruction:

> 業從何來。業往何去。誰是業者。

"Where does karma come from? Where does karma go? Who is the one with karma?"

Upon investigation, no substantial karma or karma-bearer can be located.

#### Mode 5: Discerning Openness and Obstruction (識通塞)

> 執業即塞。了業空即通。

"Grasping karma is obstruction. Understanding karma as empty is openness."

The diagnostic function determines whether karmic manifestation obstructs or opens the path.

#### Modes 6-10: Complete Application

The remaining modes are applied:

- **Mode 6** (調道品): Adjust path-factors according to karmic conditions
- **Mode 7** (助道對治): Apply specific antidotes (四力) to karmic obstacles
- **Mode 8** (識次位): Recognize one's stage relative to karmic purification
- **Mode 9** (能安忍): Endure karmic manifestations with patience
- **Mode 10** (無法愛): Avoid attachment to states of purification

### VII. The Ultimate Purification

Miao-lo presents the highest teaching on karma purification:

> 業性本空。何須更滅。了業即空。業即解脫。

"The nature of karma is fundamentally empty. What need is there to extinguish it further? Understanding karma as empty—karma is itself liberation."

This corresponds to the *Śikṣāsamuccaya*'s ultimate teaching: "True purification is seeing 'transgression as no-transgression.'"

> 若了諸法本來清淨。無有自性。則雖造惡業。不墮惡道。

"If one understands that all dharmas are fundamentally pure and without self-nature, then even having created evil karma, one does not fall into evil paths."

However, Miao-lo immediately guards against misunderstanding:

> 非謂縱任。乃是真實見業空故。

"This does not mean indulgence. It is because one truly sees that karma is empty."

This realization must be genuine insight, not intellectual concept used to excuse behavior.

### VIII. Special Cases: Heavy Karma

For particularly heavy karma (such as the five heinous acts), Miao-lo prescribes intensified methods:

> 若造五逆。當勤修懺悔。求佛加護。

"If one has committed the five heinous acts, one should diligently practice repentance and seek the Buddha's protective blessing."

Specific methods include:

1. **Recitation of Buddha names**: Especially the 35 Buddhas or Medicine Buddha
2. **Dharani recitation**: Protective mantras such as the Cundī Dhāraṇī
3. **Invoking Ākāśagarbha**: For confession of root downfalls
4. **Stupa offerings**: Even a single flower can prevent lower rebirth

### IX. Doctrinal Significance

The Karma Object (業境) completes the triad of internal obstacles:
- **Object 2** (煩惱境): Mental afflictions
- **Object 3** (病患境): Physical illness
- **Object 4** (業境): Karmic manifestations

Together, these three address what arises from within the practitioner during contemplation. The remaining objects (5-10) address external phenomena and advanced stages.

The Tiantai approach to karma is distinctive:

> 不同小乘斷業。亦不同外道自然。乃是圓教即業論空。

"This is not like the Hīnayāna severance of karma, nor like the non-Buddhist doctrine of naturalism. It is the Perfect Teaching's [approach of] understanding karma as empty."

The practitioner neither eliminates karma through ascetic effort nor ignores it through philosophical dismissal, but penetrates to its empty nature while respecting its functional power.

---

## Key Technical Terms

| Chinese | Pinyin | Definition |
|---------|--------|------------|
| 業境 | yè jìng | Karma Object |
| 業相 | yè xiàng | Karmic signs |
| 定業 | dìng yè | Fixed karma |
| 不定業 | bù dìng yè | Unfixed karma |
| 四力 | sì lì | Four powers (of purification) |
| 追悔力 | zhuī huǐ lì | Power of revulsion |
| 對治力 | duì zhì lì | Power of antidote |
| 遮止力 | zhē zhǐ lì | Power of restraint |
| 依止力 | yī zhǐ lì | Power of support |
| 五逆 | wǔ nì | Five heinous acts |
| 業性本空 | yè xìng běn kōng | Nature of karma fundamentally empty |
| 懺悔 | chàn huǐ | Repentance |

---

## Cross-References

- **Indian Sources**: The four powers align with *Śikṣāsamuccaya* Ch. 8 (Pāpaśodhana); karmic signs align with the *Cundādhāraṇī* teaching; ultimate purification aligns with *Tathāgatakoṣa Sūtra*
- **Tiantai Context**: This section completes Objects 2-4 (internal obstacles) and prepares for Objects 5-7 (external obstacles)
- **Lotus Sūtra Connection**: The teaching that "karma is empty" derives from the One Vehicle doctrine wherein all phenomena are embraced within the path

---

**END OF SECTION 3**



---



<!-- FASCICLE 08 CLOSING -->

# Fascicle 8: Closing Summary — The Three Internal Obstacles
## Scholarly Translation

**Source**: T46n1912, Fascicle 8 (卷第八)
**Author**: Miao-lo (Zhanran, 湛然, 711-782 CE)
**Translator**: William Altig / Claude
**Date**: January 23, 2026

**Five Flavors Assessment**: Ghee (法華涅槃) — Obstacles as Buddha-nature
**Six Stages Location**: Practice (修行即) — Active processing complete

---

## Summary: The Architecture of Objects 2-4

Fascicle 8 completes the exposition of the three **internal obstacles** that arise during contemplation:

| Object | Chinese | Domain | Content |
|--------|---------|--------|---------|
| 2. Affliction | 煩惱境 | Mind | Three poisons, five coverings, eight kinds of arrogance |
| 3. Illness | 病患境 | Body | Four-element imbalance, six causes, six treatments |
| 4. Karma | 業境 | Action | Past karma manifesting, four powers of purification |

These three objects correspond to the traditional Three Obstacles (三障) from the *Mahāparinirvāṇa Sūtra*:

| Obstacle | Objects | Domain |
|----------|---------|--------|
| Affliction Obstacle (煩惱障) | Object 2 | Mental defilements |
| Karma Obstacle (業障) | Object 4 | Past actions |
| Retribution Obstacle (報障) | Object 3 | Bodily conditions |

---

## The Transition from Method to Application

Fascicle 8 marks the critical transition from the **Ten Modes** (methodology) to the **Ten Objects** (application):

### What Fascicles 5-7 Established

The Ten Modes of contemplation:
1. Contemplating the inconceivable object (一念三千)
2. Arousing the bodhi-mind
3. Skillfully settling the mind
4. Breaking through all dharmas
5. Discerning openness and obstruction
6. Adjusting the path-factors
7. Counteractive aids for opening
8. Knowing the sequential positions
9. Patient endurance
10. Freedom from dharma-attachment

### What Fascicle 8 Demonstrates

How to **apply** these ten methods when the practitioner encounters:
- Mental disturbance (afflictions intensifying)
- Physical disturbance (illness arising)
- Karmic disturbance (past actions manifesting)

Each object receives:
1. Classification of types and causes
2. Treatment methods (gradual and sudden)
3. Application of all ten modes
4. Ultimate integration (empty, provisional, middle)

---

## The Structure of Treatment

### Gradual Treatment (思議)

Each object has specific antidotes:

**Afflictions**:
| Affliction | Antidote |
|------------|----------|
| Greed | Impurity contemplation |
| Hatred | Loving-kindness contemplation |
| Delusion | Dependent origination contemplation |

**Illness**:
| Cause | Treatment |
|-------|-----------|
| Element imbalance | Breath regulation, visualization |
| Diet | Dietary adjustment |
| Meditation error | Posture and method correction |
| Karmic | Contemplative acceptance |
| Demonic | Mantras, protection |

**Karma**:
| Power | Application |
|-------|-------------|
| Revulsion | Acknowledge with remorse |
| Antidote | Practice positive actions |
| Restraint | Vow not to repeat |
| Support | Rely on Three Treasures |

### Sudden Treatment (不思議)

All three objects receive the same ultimate treatment:

> 煩惱即菩提。病即法界。業性本空。

"Afflictions are precisely bodhi. Illness is precisely the dharma-realm. The nature of karma is fundamentally empty."

This is not philosophical bypassing but genuine penetration to the empty nature of each obstacle.

---

## The Relationship of Objects to Modes

Miao-lo clarifies the structural relationship:

> 十境非十乘。十乘觀十境。

"The Ten Objects are not the Ten Modes. The Ten Modes contemplate the Ten Objects."

The relationship is:

| Component | Function |
|-----------|----------|
| Ten Modes | The methodology (how to contemplate) |
| Ten Objects | The phenomena (what is contemplated) |

Each object receives all ten modes applied to it. Therefore:
- Object 2 (Affliction) × 10 Modes = 10 applications
- Object 3 (Illness) × 10 Modes = 10 applications
- Object 4 (Karma) × 10 Modes = 10 applications

---

## Cross-References to Indian Sources

Fascicle 8's teachings align with the *Śikṣāsamuccaya* on multiple points:

### Affliction Object
- Three poisons arising through "unwise attention" (ayoniśomanaskāra)
- Specific antidotes (pratipakṣa) for specific afflictions
- Ultimate teaching: "By understanding afflictions, there is bodhi"

### Illness Object
- Body as impure collection of elements
- Medicine taken "without attachment to taste"
- Body as vehicle for practice, not abandoned but transformed

### Karma Object
- Four powers of purification (Caturdharmaka)
- Karmic signs appearing in dreams during purification
- Ultimate realization: "transgression as no-transgression"

---

## The Integration of Three Truths

Each object is ultimately perceived through the Three Truths:

| Object | Empty | Provisional | Middle |
|--------|-------|-------------|--------|
| Affliction | No inherent existence | Functions as defilement | Neither grasped nor rejected |
| Illness | No real disease | Functions as condition | Neither fled nor cultivated |
| Karma | No substantial action | Functions as cause-effect | Neither eliminated nor indulged |

The practitioner applies this threefold perception simultaneously, not sequentially.

---

## Preparation for Fascicle 9

Having completed the three internal obstacles, Miao-lo will address the **external obstacles** in Fascicle 9:

| Object | Chinese | Domain |
|--------|---------|--------|
| 5. Demons | 魔事境 | External interference |
| 6. Meditative States | 禪定境 | Attainment as obstacle |
| 7. Wrong Views | 邪見境 | Mistaken understanding |

These three require different treatment because they involve phenomena from outside the practitioner's immediate experience.

---

## Key Technical Terms Across Fascicle 8

| Chinese | Pinyin | Definition |
|---------|--------|------------|
| 十境 | shí jìng | Ten Objects |
| 三障 | sān zhàng | Three Obstacles |
| 煩惱境 | fán nǎo jìng | Affliction Object |
| 病患境 | bìng huàn jìng | Illness Object |
| 業境 | yè jìng | Karma Object |
| 思議 | sī yì | Conceivable (gradual treatment) |
| 不思議 | bù sī yì | Inconceivable (sudden treatment) |
| 對治 | duì zhì | Antidote |
| 四力 | sì lì | Four Powers |
| 六氣 | liù qì | Six Healing Breaths |
| 業性本空 | yè xìng běn kōng | Nature of karma fundamentally empty |
| 煩惱即菩提 | fán nǎo jí pú tí | Afflictions are precisely bodhi |

---

## Doctrinal Significance

Fascicle 8 establishes the foundational Tiantai principle for working with obstacles:

> 障即是道。無障可離。

"Obstacles are precisely the path. There are no obstacles to leave behind."

This does not mean obstacles are ignored or indulged, but that they are the very material through which realization occurs. The practitioner who encounters afflictions, illness, or karma during practice has not failed—they have encountered the path itself.

The Perfect Teaching (圓教) integrates all phenomena within the single vehicle. Nothing is excluded; nothing is merely negative; everything becomes the gateway.

---

## Files in Fascicle 8 Scholarly Series

1. `Fascicle_08_Opening_Scholarly.md` — Introduction to Ten Objects
2. `Fascicle_08_Section_01_Scholarly.md` — Affliction Object (煩惱境)
3. `Fascicle_08_Section_02_Scholarly.md` — Illness Object (病患境)
4. `Fascicle_08_Section_03_Scholarly.md` — Karma Object (業境)
5. `Fascicle_08_Closing_Summary_Scholarly.md` — Integration and summary (this file)

---

**END OF FASCICLE 8 SCHOLARLY TRANSLATION**

---
